# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Leader Election Patterns Across K8s Ecosystem

## Your Task

Compare leader election implementations across kubernetes/kubernetes and etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that implement leader election: the lease-based election in k8s, the Raft-based leader in etcd, and how each handles leader failover and re-election.

42-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive comparison of leader election implementations across the Kubernetes and etcd codebases. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've documented **6 key source files** implementing leader election in both systems:

### **Kubernetes (Lease-Based Election)**
- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go` - Core `LeaderElector` implementation with `Run()`, `acquire()`, `renew()`, and `tryAcquireOrRenew()` methods
- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go` - Lease resource lock using Kubernetes API objects
- `pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/run_with_leaderelection.go` - Integration with controller managers

**Key mechanism**: Time-based lease renewal with configurable timers (LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod). Failover occurs when a leader fails to renew its lease within the deadline.

### **etcd (Raft-Based Election)**
- `server/etcdserver/raft.go` - `raftNode` wrapper implementing tick-based Raft state machine
- `client/v3/concurrency/election.go` - Client-side `Election` library with `Campaign()`, `Proclaim()`, and `Resign()` methods
- `server/etcdserver/api/v3election/election.go` - Server-side election RPC implementation

**Key mechanism**: Raft consensus algorithm with automatic leader election triggered by heartbeat timeouts. Provides strong consistency guarantees through quorum-based voting.

## Critical Differences

- **Speed**: K8s failover is ~15 seconds (default LeaseDuration), while etcd is sub-second via election timeout
- **Guarantees**: K8s is time-based with no strict fencing; etcd uses Raft for strong consistency and safety
- **Use Cases**: K8s is for distributed controller management; etcd is for cluster-critical consensus

This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. \\n71: const (\\n72: \\tJitterFactor = 1.2\\n73: )\\n74: \\n75: // NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\\n76: func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\\n226: // stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\\n227: func RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\\n228: \\tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\\n229: \\tif err != nil {\\n230: \\t\\tpanic(err)\\n231: \\t}\\n232: \\tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\\n233: \\t\\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\\n234: \\t}\\n235: \\tle.Run(ctx)\\n236: }\\n237: \\n238: // GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\\n239: // no leader has yet been observed.\\n240: // This function is for informational purposes.     "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n21: //\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n29: //\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n37: //\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n41: // availability.\n42: //\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n48: // to master availability.\n49: //\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n52: // your own risk.\n53: package leaderelection\n54: \n55: import (\n56: \t\"bytes\"\n57: \t\"context\"\n58: \t\"fmt\"\n59: \t\"sync\"\n60: \t\"time\"\n61: \n62: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n63: \tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n64: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n65: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n66: \trl \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n67: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n68: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n69: )\n70: \n71: const (\n72: \tJitterFactor = 1.2\n73: )\n74: \n75: // NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n76: func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n77: \tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n78: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n79: \t}\n80: \tif lec.RenewDeadline <= time.Duration(JitterFactor*float64(lec.RetryPeriod)) {\n81: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n82: \t}\n83: \tif lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n84: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n85: \t}\n86: \tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n87: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n88: \t}\n89: \tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n90: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"retryPeriod must be greater than zero\")\n91: \t}\n92: \tif lec.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading == nil {\n93: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStartedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n94: \t}\n95: \tif lec.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading == nil {\n96: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStoppedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n97: \t}\n98: \n99: \tif lec.Lock == nil {\n100: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock must not be nil.\")\n101: \t}\n102: \tid := lec.Lock.Identity()\n103: \tif id == \"\" {\n104: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock identity is empty\")\n105: \t}\n106: \n107: \tle := LeaderElector{\n108: \t\tconfig:  lec,\n109: \t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n110: \t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n111: \t}\n112: \tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n113: \treturn &le, nil\n114: }\n115: \n116: type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\n117: \t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\n118: \tLock rl.Interface\n119: \n120: \t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\n121: \t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n122: \t// last observed ack.\n123: \t//\n124: \t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n125: \t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n126: \t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n127: \t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n128: \t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n129: \t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n130: \t// long waits in the scenario.\n131: \t//\n132: \t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n133: \tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n134: \t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n135: \t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n136: \t//\n137: \t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n138: \tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n139: \t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n140: \t// between tries of actions.\n141: \t//\n142: \t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n143: \tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n144: \n145: \t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n146: \t// events of the LeaderElector\n147: \tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n148: \n149: \t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n150: \t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n151: \tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n152: \n153: \t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n154: \t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n155: \t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n156: \t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n157: \t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n158: \tReleaseOnCancel bool\n159: \n160: \t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n161: \tName string\n162: \n163: \t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n164: \t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n165: \tCoordinated bool\n166: }\n167: \n168: // LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n169: // lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n170: //\n171: // possible future callbacks:\n172: //   - OnChallenge()\n173: type LeaderCallbacks struct {\n174: \t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n175: \tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n176: \t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n177: \t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n178: \t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n179: \t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n180: \tOnStoppedLeading func()\n181: \t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n182: \t// not the previously observed leader. Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election through a **lease-based mechanism** in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`. The core component is the `LeaderElector` struct, which manages a leadership claim on a Kubernetes Lease resource.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Election Flow\\n\\nThe election process follows this sequence:\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: `NewLeaderElector()` creates a LeaderElector with a `LeaderElectionConfig` containing:\\n   - `Lock`: A `LeaseLock` (defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go`) that represents a Kubernetes Lease API object\\n   - `LeaseDuration`: How long the lease is valid (default 15 seconds)\\n   - `RenewDeadline`: Time to renew before giving up (default 10 seconds)\\n   - `RetryPeriod`: Interval between retries (default 2 seconds)\\n\\n2. **Leadership Acquisition**: `LeaderElector.Run()` calls `acquire()`, which repeatedly calls `tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx)` until successful. This method:\\n   - Attempts to create a new LeaderElectionRecord in the Lease if it doesn't exist\\n   - Updates the Lease with HolderIdentity, AcquireTime, and RenewTime fields\\n   - Uses fast-path optimization: if already leading, optimistically updates the record\\n   - Falls back to slow-path (full read-modify-write) on conflict\\n\\n3. **Leadership Renewal**: Once acquired, `Run()` calls `renew()`, which continuously attempts to renew the lease within `RenewDeadline` using `PollUntilContextTimeout()`. The renewal checks:\\n   - `isLeaseValid()` verifies the lease hasn't expired by checking: `observedTime + LeaseDurationSeconds > now`\\n   - If renewal fails within RenewDeadline, the process stops leading\\n\\n### Kubernetes Failover and Re-election\\n\\nFailover is **time-based** and deterministic:\\n\\n1. **Leader Detection**: When a leader dies, no renewal happens. Other candidates wait for `LeaseDuration` to expire (time since last successful renewal).\\n2. **Re-election Trigger**: Once `LeaseDuration` expires, any candidate can call `tryAcquireOrRenew()` which checks: if `len(HolderIdentity) > 0 && isLeaseValid(now) && !IsLeader()` returns false (lease expired), it attempts to acquire.\\n3. **Transition Tracking**: `maybeReportTransition()` triggers the `OnNewLeader()` callback when leadership changes detected through `LeaderElectionRecord.HolderIdentity`.\\n\\nThe implementation explicitly documents that it does NOT provide strict fencing (only one holder), relying instead on timestamps and local clocks. It's tolerant to clock skew but not to high clock skew rates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election through the **Raft consensus algorithm** at the server level, with an optional client-side election API wrapper.\\n\\n### etcd Server-Level Raft Election\\n\\nThe core Raft implementation is in `server/etcdserver/raft.go` in the `raftNode` struct:\\n\\n1. **Node Initialization**: `newRaftNode(cfg raftNodeConfig)` creates a raftNode that wraps a `raft.Node` with:\\n   - Periodic `tick()` calls (based on heartbeat interval, typically ~100ms)\\n   - A transport layer for sending/receiving Raft messages\\n   - Storage layer for persisting Raft state\\n\\n2. **Election Loop**: `raftNode.start()` launches a goroutine that:\\n   - Calls `tick()` on each heartbeat ticker interval\\n   - Processes `Ready()` states from the Raft node\\n   - Detects leadership changes via `rd.SoftState.Lead`\\n   - Calls `updateLeadership(newLeader)` when leadership transitions occur\\n   - The Raft state machine internally handles campaign timeout logic\\n\\n3. **Leadership State**: Leadership is determined by the Raft node's internal state:\\n   - `rd.RaftState == raft.StateLeader` indicates the node is now leader\\n   - `rd.SoftState.Lead` contains the leader's node ID\\n   - Metrics track: `isLeader.Set(1)` for leader, `leaderChanges.Inc()` on transitions\\n\\n### etcd Client-Side Election API\\n\\nFor application-level leader election, etcd provides `client/v3/concurrency/election.go`:\\n\\n1. **Campaign**: `Election.Campaign(ctx, val)` implements client-side election:\\n   - Uses a transaction: `If(v3.Compare(v3.CreateRevision(k), \\\"=\\\", 0))`\\n   - Puts a key `\\\"%s%x\\\".format(keyPrefix, lease_id)` with the election value\\n   - Waits for all keys with lower CreateRevision to be deleted via `waitDeletes()`\\n   - Only becomes leader when all previous candidates resign\\n\\n2. **Proclaim**: `Election.Proclaim(ctx, val)` allows leader to announce new values with transactional safety\\n\\n3. **Resign**: `Election.Resign(ctx)` releases leadership, allowing next candidate to become leader\\n\\n### etcd Failover and Re-election\\n\\nFailover is **automatic and consensus-based**:\\n\\n1. **Failure Detection**: When a leader fails:\\n   - Followers stop receiving heartbeats within election timeout (~150-300ms in Raft)\\n   - The Raft state machine automatically initiates `Campaign()` internally\\n   - Raft protocol ensures safe state transitions through majority quorum\\n\\n2. **Leader Election**: The Raft consensus algorithm guarantees:\\n   - A term increments on each election\\n   - A node becomes candidate, increments term, and sends RequestVote RPCs\\n   - First candidate to get majority votes becomes leader\\n   - All entries from previous leader are committed before new entries\\n\\n3. **Leadership Transition Detection**: `server/etcdserver/raft.go` lines 186-204:\\n   - `newLeader := rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None && rh.getLead() != rd.SoftState.Lead`\\n   - On transition: `leaderChanges.Inc()` and `hasLeader.Set(1/0)`\\n   - Resets contention detector with `r.td.Reset()`\\n\\n4. **Member Changes**: Configuration changes are replayed as `raftpb.EntryConfChange` entries before followers can participate, ensuring consistency during membership updates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Lease-based on API objects | Raft consensus algorithm |\\n| **Failure Detection** | Time-based (LeaseDuration) | Election timeout (async heartbeat) |\\n| **Failover Speed** | Deterministic, ~LeaseDuration (15s default) | Sub-second (depends on election timeout) |\\n| **Fencing** | Not guaranteed (time-based only) | Strong consistency via quorum |\\n| **Storage** | Kubernetes Lease API | Raft log + persistent storage |\\n| **Applicability** | Controller managers, schedulers | Cluster-wide consensus, core state |\\n| **Client Integration** | Uses Lock interface with retries | Raft consensus integrated in server |\\n\"",

A term increments on each election\\n   - A node becomes candidate, increments term, and sends RequestVote RPCs\\n   - First candidate to get majority votes becomes leader\\n   - All entries from previous leader are committed before new entries\\n\\n3. **Leadership Transition Detection**: `server/etcdserver/raft.go` lines 186-204:\\n   - `newLeader := rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None && rh.getLead() != rd.SoftState.Lead`\\n   - On transition: `leaderChanges.Inc()` and `hasLeader.Set(1/0)`\\n   - Resets contention detector with `r.td.Reset()`\\n\\n4. **Member Changes**: Configuration changes are replayed as `raftpb.EntryConfChange` entries before followers can participate, ensuring consistency during membership updates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Lease-based on API objects | Raft consensus algorithm |\\n| **Failure Detection** | Time-based (LeaseDuration) | Election timeout (async heartbeat) |\\n| **Failover Speed** | Deterministic, ~LeaseDuration (15s default) | Sub-second (depends on election timeout) |\\n| **Fencing** | Not guaranteed (time-based only) | Strong consistency via quorum |\\n| **Storage** | Kubernetes Lease API | Raft log + persistent storage |\\n| **Applicability** | Controller managers, schedulers | Cluster-wide consensus, core state |\\n| **Client Integration** | Uses Lock interface with retries | Raft consensus integrated in server |\\n\"",
  "filePath": "/workspace/answer.json",

  "type": "create"
}
